הבחורים שדיברו עמהם אודות לימוד להוראה [חלקם הנני רואה כאן, הנשארים אינני רואה, ובודאי ימסרו את הדברים גם אליהם] - הרי לא לדרשא קאתינא, אלא הכוונה היא בנוגע *לפועל ממש*;
וגם הבחורים שלא דיברו עמהם על כך, אבל הם ראויים ומוכשרים לזה - יקבלו את הדבר על עצמם, ובפועל ממש, מתחיל מלילה זה או מחר בבוקר, ייגשו אל העבודה ("צוטרעטן צו דער ארבעט") - בהתאם לסדרי הישיבה ושאר הלימודים שמחוייבים בהם (הן לימודים בחסידות והן לימודים בנגלה) - וישלימו הלימוד להוראה עד לחג הפסח, ועכ"פ לא יאוחר מחג השבועות.
ועד"ז בנוגע להבעה"ב הראויים לכך - ה"ז דבר נכון ביותר שגם הם יהיו בקיאים בהוראה, ותבוא עליהם ברכה.
כב. שמעתי פעם מכ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר, שמנהג בית הרב הי' לקבל סמיכה להוראה קודם החתונה[ftnref\_1384\_110], וכך נהג גם הוא בעצמו:נישואי כ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר התקיימו בהיותו בן שבע עשרה שנה, ולפני זה, למד במיוחד עבור הוראה. - לפני תקופה זו, למד בתור לימוד התורה סתם (ולא בשביל הוראה וכיו"ב), אבל קודם החתונה רצה כ"ק אדמו"ר (מהורש"ב) נ"ע שיקבל סמיכה, ואכן קיבל אז סמיכה אצל כמה רבנים.
- (כ"ק אדמו"ר שליט"א חייך ואמר:) כנראה, שהרבנים ייגעו אותו קשות ("זיי האבן אים גוט געמאטערט"), וכשנוכחו לדעת שאכן ראוי הוא לכך, "ער האט דאס כשר פארדינט", לא באופן של "נהמא דכיסופא"[ftnref\_1322\_48], אלא ע"י יגיעה ("יגעת"[ftnref\_1385\_111]), נתנו לו הסמיכה...
ואף שהמדובר הוא בנוגע להנהגה של בית הרב, מ"מ, כיון שכ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר סיפר וגילה את הדבר,
- כבר אמרתי פעם, שכאשר כ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר הי' מספר לי סיפור, כבר ידע מלכתחילה שאפרסם אותו, "פריער מיט א טאג שפעטער מיט א טאג", אם בעל פה, או בכתב, או בדפוס, אבל זאת ידע, שהדבר לא יישאר בגדר סוד;
אלא שבזה גופא היו חילוקים: היו ענינים כאלה - שציוה עלי להעלימם לעצמי ("באהאלטן פאר זיך"), ואזי הייתי צריך לבקש ולפעול ("אויסבעטן") רשיון על פירסום הדבר; אבל היו גם ענינים שמלכתחילה לא הטיל עליהם "הגבלות" -
מובן, שמנהג זה הוא *הוראה לרבים* - שצריכים לקבל סמיכה להוראה קודם החתונה.
וטעם הדבר - כיון שלעתים תכופות מתעוררות בבית שאלות שונות בהלכה, ואי אפשר ללכת לעתים קרובות כל כך לשאול את הרב ("מ'קען דאך ניט לויפן יעדן פאר מינוט צו א רב"), ולכך צריך להיות רב בתוך הבית.
כג. ובהתאם לכך יש לעורר - שכדאי ונכון ביותר שכאו"א הרוצה לבנות "בנין עדי עד"[ftnref\_1386\_112] (ועד"ז אברכים ובעה"ב שלאחרי החתונה) - יוציא תחילה סמיכה להוראה. ובודאי יש ביכלתו של כאו"א לקבל סמיכה - לכל הפחות כפי הסדר הנהוג בזמננו זה:
בזמנים שעברו ידעו שכדי לקבל סמיכה לרבנות - הרי לכל לראש "דארף מען גוט קענען לערנען", ולאחרי זה יש לדעת כדבעי טורושולחן ערוך, כל חלקיהם, או לכל הפחות שני חלקים - יורה דעה ואבן העזר;
ואילו בזמננו זה נעשה הסדר, שמתחילים בלימוד קיצור שו"ע, ולאח"ז מוסיפים ולומדים פי' הבאר-היטב, ולאח"ז מוסיפים ולומדים שו"ע עם פירושי הט"ז והש"ך, ולאחרי זה אם זמנו פנוי - מוסיפים ולומדים טור וב"י, וגם זה - רק קטעים קטעים.
ובכן, כוונתי לקבל סמיכה לכל הפחות באופן כזה - כדי לדעת את המעשה אשר יעשון, אשר לשם כך צריכה להיות ידיעה בשו"ע אורח חיים ויורה דעה, וגם איזו ידיעה בענינים דאבן העזר, אבל, לכל לראש ולכל הפחות - או"ח ויו"ד, שמוכרח הוא באם רוצים לדעת את המעשה אשר יעשון, ולא להכשל ח"ו בכו"כ הלכות, כמו הלכות שבת (כמ"ש רבינו הזקן באגרת הקודש[ftnref\_1298\_24]) וכיו"ב.
ויש להדגיש, שלא נוגע כ"כ קבלת התעודה ("די פאפירל") בצירוף חתימה המעידה על קבלת הסמיכה, כי אם, *היכולת* לקבל תעודה כזו, ומאחר *שראוי* לכך, התעודה עצמה כבר אינה מעכבת, ובלשון חז"ל[ftnref\_1387\_113] "הראוי לבילה אין בילה מעכבת בו".
אלא שבנוגע להבחורים דורשים בפירוש שיקבלו גם את התעודה, שכן, עי"ז יוכלו לדעת שמילאו את תפקידם (ללמוד כל הלכות המתאימות) בפועל. ומה טוב שישלחום להבחן אצל מישהו ש"מחמיר" בנתינת הסמיכה, שאז יתברר שמילאו את תפקידם (בלימוד ההלכות) *כדבעי*[ftnref\_1388\_114].
כד. ויש לקשר גם ענין זה עם יום ההילולא כ"ד טבת:
מעניניו העיקריים של בעל ההילולא ובעל השמחה הי' חיבור *השולחן-ערוך*, כידוע[ftnref\_1389\_115] שבבוא רבינו הזקן למעזריטש נמסר לו התפקיד של חיבור השו"ע לרבים - לא רק בשביל חסידים אלא גם עבור כלל ישראל [ביחד עם יסוד ופירסום של תורת חסידות חב"ד לכלל ישראל[ftnref\_1318\_44]].
ומזה מובן, שכאשר מקבלים החלטות טובות בכל האמור ביום ההילולא - ישנו סיוע מיוחד לקיים את ההחלטה בפועל, ושתהי' הצלחה בזמן, הצלחה ברוחניות, והצלחה בגשמיות.
\*\*\*כה. [כ"ק אדמו"ר שליט"א צוה לנגן (באמרו שהשעה היא כבר לאחרי חצות) ניגון ד' בבות של רבינו הזקן, ובבא הרביעית - לכפול ז' פעמים. לאחרי שניגנו ניגון ד' הבבות, אמר: "זאל מען זינגען דעם ניגון "ניע זשוריצי כלאפצי", נאר פריילעך".
במהלך הניגון עמד כ"ק אדמו"ר שליט"א מלוא קומתו ורקד (ביחד עם כל הקהל שנעמד על הספסלים והשולחנות) בשמחה רבה ועצומה.
ואח"כ אמר:]
בודאי אין צורך להבהיר ולהדגיש שאי אפשר לצאת ידי חובה בהנ"ל[ftnref\_1390\_116], שכן, כל זה אינו אלא הכנה והקדמה לקיום מצוות מעשיות כפשוטו, ובפרטיות, לקביעות עתים בתורת הנגלה ובתורת החסידות, ובקשר לתלמידי הישיבה - שקידה והתמדה נוספת הן בלימוד הנגלה והן בלימוד החסידות.
- זהו ענין של בפועל ממש, שאפשר למשש ולמדוד ע"פ השעון... במילא לא יתכן לרמות את הזולת בענין זה, ולא עוד, אלא שגם את עצמו אי אפשר לרמות בכך!...
ולהוסיף ולהדגיש, שאין זה ענין הנוגע לאחר זמן, כי אם, מחר בבוקר בפועל ממש!
- בנוגע ללילה זה, הרי מכיון שנמצאים כבר לאחרי חצות הלילה, ה"ז שייך לחשבונו של יום המחרת.
\*
כו. כאן המקום לעורר גם אודות ההכנות ליום ההילולא של כ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר:
ובהקדמה[ftnref\_1391\_117] - שכל ההשפעות השייכות אלינו מקבלים אנו על ידי ממוצע המחבר, הוא כ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר[ftnref\_1392\_118], ועל ידו נמשכים אלינו גם כל הענינים דיום ההילולא של רבינו הזקן, להתקשר ולהתאחד עמו וכו'.
וכיון שנשארו חמשה עשר יום עד לה"יארצייט", יום ההילולא של נשיאינו, ובמענה על שאלת כו"כ אודות הסדר ביום זה - הצעתי, שסדרההנהגה ביום ההילולא בשנה זו יהי' - במדה האפשרית - כפי ההצעה שנכתבה אשתקד[ftnref\_1393\_119], ובודאי יוכלו למלאותה גם בשנה זו.
- הסיבה שהנני מדבר על כך בהזדמנות זו, היא, בגלל שגם כעת עומדים אנו ביום הילולא (של רבינו הזקן). ונוסף לכך, מכיון שישנם כו"כ שכבר שאלו אצלם אודות הסדר של יום ההילולא, וזקוקים הם ליתן מענה על כך, הרי, אלו ששואלים את הצעתי - כבר מלתי אמורה בהסדר שנכתב בשנה שעברה,
ובפרטיות יותר - הן בנוגע לעלי' לתורה בשבת קודש שלפני יום ההילולא, ועד"ז בנוגע לסדר ההנהגה ביום ההילולא עצמו.
וגם כשיעזור הקב"ה שעד אז כבר תהי' ביאת משיח צדקנו, ומה גם[ftnref\_1394\_120] ש"הקיצו ורננו שוכני עפר"[ftnref\_1395\_121], והוא בתוכם, יכול להיות עוד לפנ"ז, ויש כמה ראיות בש"ס ומדרשים שיכול להיות הענין ד"הקיצו ורננו" אצל יחידי סגולה לפנ"ז, וגם הי' לפנ"ז; ובפרט כאשר המדובר בנוגע לנשיא שצריך להוציא את צאן מרעיתו מחושך כפול ומכופל כזה -
אין זה מבלבל לסדר האמור ביום ההילולא, כיון שגם אז יהי' זה יום ההילולא, ומה איכפת ("וואס הארט") אם זה באופן למטה מעשרה טפחים או למעלה מעשרה טפחים?! - וכיון שאין סתירה בדבר, יכול להיות הסדר כדאשתקד.
כז. [בסיום ההתוועדות אמר כ"ק אדמו"ר שליט"א (בחיוך):]
בהמשך להמדובר אודות ההדגשה דנגלה דתורה - "ס'איז דאך אלץ א נאכט פון נגלה"... - יש להזכיר ולעורר שכל אלה שנתחייבו בברכה אחרונה לא ישכחו לברך ברכה אחרונה[ftnref\_1396\_122]; ואלה שאינם יודעים את הברכה בעל-פה, אל יתביישו לברך מתוך הסידור, ותבוא עליהם ברכה, ואנחנו נאמר ("און מיר וועלן ענטפערן") אמן.
[כ"ק אדמו"ר שליט"א הזכיר עוד הפעם אודות חלוקת הש"ס, באמרו, שכל אלה שהשתתפו בחלוקת הש"ס יודיעו איזו מסכתא בוחרים הם ללמוד, ובמילא יצרפו אותם לחלוקה הכללית, ושכל המשתתפים יזכרו את המסכתא שקיבלו על עצמם ללמוד, ויגמרו אותה עד לשנה הבע"ל.
ואח"כ אמר:]תכליתה של התוועדות חסידית היא - שההחלטות טובות שמחליטים בעת ההתוועדות תפעלנה בפועל ממש במחשבה דיבור ומעשה, להמשיך את אור החסידות במחשבה דיבור ומעשה, בכל יום ויום, ועל ידי כך יאיר כאו"א עוד יותר את חלקו בעולם, וכולם ביחד - את כל העולם.
[וסיים כ"ק אדמו"ר שליט"א:] "זייט געזונט און א גוטע נאכט"[ftnref\_1397\_123].
------- \* -------

**English:**

## Sicha of Tuesday, Parshas Va’era, 24 Teves, 5712

**Unedited**

**1.** [The Rebbe instructed that a *Shas* distribution be organized using the designated cards. After the cards were distributed and the *Shas* was divided, the Rebbe said:]

The Rebbe Maharash writes in one of his *maamarim* that "at the very least, everyone should study one tractate of Gemara per year."

This study can be done individually, but it can also be done *together with the entire community*. In that case, the benefit is twofold: each of the learners takes a share in the study of the others and gives a share of his own study to all the others. Both the individual and the community benefit from this.

Consequently, everyone can join the *Shas* distribution currently being organized, where each person studies the tractate he accepts upon himself—in conjunction with the entire public—and the merit of the many assists them.

[The Rebbe instructed to announce that those who had not yet participated in the *Shas* distribution should do so now.]

**2.** (After Rabbi Meir Ashkenazi finished the *Shas*, the Rebbe said:) It is customary to conduct a *Hadran* on the *Shas*.

The *Hadran* on the *Shas*—an explanation of the dispute between Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel regarding whether a woman who sees blood on the eleventh day is considered to be observing a day by Torah law, and the dispute between Rabbi Yochanan and Reish Lakish (regarding the view of Beis Hillel) as to whether she is obligated to observe a day if she sees blood on the tenth—is based on their respective positions regarding whether a "half-measure" (*chatzi shiur*) is prohibited by Torah law. The dispute between Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel is based on their respective positions regarding whether we follow the "potential" (*b'koach*) or the "actual" (*b'po'al*). [This was edited by the Rebbe and printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 107 and onwards.]

At the conclusion of the *Hadran*—in connection with the *halacha* following Beis Hillel that we follow the "actual"—the Rebbe said:

One should connect this concept (that the *halacha* follows Beis Hillel, that "potential" is insufficient and it must be "actual") with the conclusion of the *Shas* in the Gemara: "The students of the school of Eliyahu taught: Whoever studies *halachos* every day is guaranteed to be a son of the World to Come, as it is said: 'His are the *halichos* (ways) of the world'; do not read *halichos* but *halachos*."

When a Jew knows that he must conduct himself in a manner of "His are the *halichos* of the world"—to study *halachos* constantly—and he generally conducts himself this way, then even if, due to circumstances beyond his control, a specific day passes in which he did not study *halachos* in actuality, this day is included in the day (and days) preceding it. Since at that time he stood, like every Jew who observes Torah and *mitzvos*, in a state of preparation to study the next day as well (if it were only within his ability), it turns out that the day preceding it already contains the "*potential*" for the study of this day as well, only that due to a cause not his fault, it did not come into actuality.

However, since the *halacha* follows Beis Hillel that it must be "actual" specifically, and also in laws pertaining to the matter of time, as in the examples explained in the *Hadran*—therefore, "The students of the school of Eliyahu taught: Whoever studies *halachos* *every day* (specifically) is guaranteed, etc.," meaning that the study of *halachos* must be *every day in actuality*. If the "actual" study of *halachos* is missing on a certain day, the "potential" of the previous day—that it was in his thought and mind to study the next day—does not suffice.

It is true that he will not be punished for not having studied *halachos* on that day because he was coerced, and "the Merciful One exempts one who is coerced," but nevertheless, we do not say "it is considered as if he did it." Since the "actual" study of *halachos* is missing for him on that day, the consequence that comes through it—"he is guaranteed, etc."—is also missing.

Only "whoever studies *halachos* every day" in actuality, then "he is guaranteed to be a son of the World to Come, as it is said: 'His are the *halichos* of the world'; do not read *halichos* but *halachos*."

***

**3.** 24 Teves is the *yahrzeit* (day of passing) of the Alter Rebbe.

24 Teves is also mentioned in the Gemara in *Bava Basra*: "On the twenty-fourth of Teves we returned to our judgment (our first trial), for the Sadducees were saying that a daughter should inherit with the daughter of the son. Rabban Yochanan ben Zakkai engaged them, etc., and defeated them, and they made that day a holiday."

However, this is a separate matter, and it has a lengthy explanation, etc., whereas the discussion now concerns us: that this day for us is the *yahrzeit* of the Alter Rebbe, and we must utilize it for everything related to walking in his ways and paths, as follows.

**4.** First and foremost—regarding the matter emphasized in his name:

Regarding the name of the Alter Rebbe—"Shneur"—it is told in the *sichos* that it hints at "two lights" (*shnei or*): "Light" refers to Torah, as it is written, "For a *mitzvah* is a candle and Torah is light." There are two categories of light: the light of the revealed Torah and the light of the teachings of Chassidus. Both together are hinted at in the name "Shneur"—one name, in which both lights are included, both the light of the revealed Torah and the light of the teachings of Chassidus.

And according to the language of the Midrash regarding the verse, "He declares His words to Jacob, His statutes and His judgments to Israel": "What He does, He tells Israel to do" (and similarly the reverse: what He commands Israel, He does)—which is also true of the *tzaddikim* who "are like their Creator," that what they do, they demand also from those who are connected and belong to them—it is understood that this is what the Alter Rebbe demands from all those who identify with and are counted among his banner and camp—after he opened and paved the way—that they too should have the unification of the light of the revealed Torah with the light of the teachings of Chassidus.

In simple terms:

The Alter Rebbe demands from each one of us both the study of the revealed Torah and the study of the teachings of Chassidus—just as he rules in the *Laws of Torah Study* regarding the obligation of every person to study Torah, that this obligation is not for a specific section of Torah, but for all sections of Torah, both the revealed Torah and the hidden Torah.

Consequently, when there are "Chassidim of the peak" who want to fulfill their obligation with this line, or conversely, "lukewarm Chassidim" who want to fulfill their obligation with that line—we say to them: *Neither this nor that*, but it must be "two lights" specifically, the two lights of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, as they are unified together specifically.

**5.** It should be added and emphasized more specifically that just as it is impossible to be satisfied with studying the revealed Torah without the hidden Torah, so too it is impossible to be satisfied with studying the hidden Torah without the revealed Torah. For the revealed Torah and the hidden Torah are like body and soul, "the bodies of Torah" and "the soul of Torah," and just as a body is impossible without a soul, so too a soul is impossible without a body (since that is not the intent), but rather the soul of Torah together with the bodies of Torah.

It should be noted that in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* in the *Tanya*, both at its beginning and at its end, the Alter Rebbe specifically demands and emphasizes the study of the revealed Torah—the *Shas* distribution: at the beginning—"the completion of the entire *Shas* in most towns and *minyanim* of *Anash*... year after year," and at the end—"to finish the entire *Shas* every year in every city, to divide the tractates, etc."

Likewise, the Rebbe Rayatz told several stories on this matter, the content of which is that the Alter Rebbe also forcefully demanded the study of the revealed Torah.

Similarly, in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by the Rebbe Rashab, he explains several details regarding the manner of studying the revealed Torah, establishing several hours a day that one must engage in the revealed Torah, just as he establishes several hours a day for the study of the teachings of Chassidus.

For this reason, they demand so forcefully from all Chassidim in general, and especially from those who are in the "tent of Torah," and from the students of the *yeshiva* in particular—that they should have extreme diligence and perseverance in the study of the revealed Torah, but that the study should be with vitality and "liveliness" (not only vitality and "liveliness" from his own understanding and grasp, but also the vitality and "liveliness" that the teachings of Chassidus add to the study of the revealed).

And the "demand" of the Rebbes is (not only a demand, but it contains) also the granting of strength, meaning that the necessary strengths were given to study the revealed and Chassidus together, in addition to the fact that the granting of strength itself obligates one to utilize the strengths to their fullest. For the lack of utilization of the strengths, *chas v'shalom*, constitutes a wrong not only toward oneself, in the sense of "one who injures himself," which, although he is not permitted, nevertheless, he is exempt, but also toward others, in the sense of "one who injures others," and all the more so when it concerns the *Nasi* of the generation!

Since this is so, it is the duty and privilege of each one to study not only the teachings of Chassidus, but also the revealed Torah (to no lesser degree), since they demand and give strength for both.

**6.** And this matter—the study of the revealed Torah with the hidden Torah, the bodies of Torah and the soul of Torah, through which a complete soul is created in a complete body—also constitutes a preparation and introduction to the complete Redemption that must be both regarding the body, the redemption of the body, and regarding the soul, the redemption of the soul.

The action of a Jew that will bring about the complete Redemption is through the completeness of his connection with Hashem, through the Torah, which is the intermediary through which the connection of Israel with Hashem is made.

And since the connection with Hashem must be in a way that the "revealed" and the "hidden" of Israel are connected with the "revealed" and the "hidden" of Hashem, there must also be his share in the Torah ("and give us our share in Your Torah," "our share" specifically) that connects Israel with Hashem, both in the "revealed" of Torah and in the "hidden" of Torah, for then the connection with Hashem is an "everlasting bond"—which is from two bonds—hidden and revealed.

And when there is an everlasting bond between Israel and Hashem, after the removal of the barrier of "your iniquities were separating between you and your God," then comes the true and complete Redemption, as the Alter Rebbe explains in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* that immediately after the blessing of "Forgive us" we bless "Redeemer of Israel"—so may it be for us speedily in our days through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

***

**7.** It was discussed above (in the *Hadran*) that there is a reasoning that the beginning of a time period includes "in potential" the continuation of the time that comes after it, but this reasoning is only according to the view of Beis Shammai, and only in the time to come will the *halacha* be according to them.

It should be added that even in this time we find that there is a time that includes several times, but the discussion is (not about the continuation of the time that comes after it, but the opposite) about the continuation of the time *that already was before it*.

And we find this matter regarding a *yahrzeit*—as the Alter Rebbe (the *baal ha-yahrzeit* of 24 Teves) explains in *Iggeres HaKodesh* that on the day of the *yahrzeit*, "all his deeds, his Torah, and his service that he performed all the days of his life" are elevated and included, meaning that the time of the *yahrzeit* includes within it the entire duration of a person's life.

**8.** And this elevation is not only at the time of the passing, but it is so also on the day of the *yahrzeit* every year.

As explained in the writings of the Arizal on the verse, "And these days are remembered and performed in every generation," that when they are "remembered" in a later generation, then all the revelations of the lights that shone in "these days" the first time return and are "performed."

From this it is also understood regarding the *yahrzeit* of the Alter Rebbe on 24 Teves, that through the remembrance ("remembered") of this day every year, all the elevations that were on the day of the passing return and are "performed"—in the words of the *baal ha-yahrzeit*—the elevation and inclusion of "all his deeds, his Torah, and his service that he (the Alter Rebbe) performed all the days of his life."

[It should be noted that this language—"his service that he performed"—is according to the language of the verse, "His work that He performed in it," which is said in the *Haftorah* of *Parshas Va’era*, in which week 24 Teves falls (in this year, and in most years, and) also the first time, as the passing was on "Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh Shemos, the 23rd, entering the 24th of Teves" (in the words of the Tzemach Tzedek), meaning, in the week of *Parshas Va’era*.]

It should be added that according to what the Alter Rebbe writes in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* (regarding an undesirable matter) that "because he is the one who continues the influence to them, therefore he takes the lead" (and all the more so in the good, for "a good measure is greater, etc.")—it is understood that all those who "remember" the day of the *yahrzeit* (and especially when they accept upon themselves matters connected with the ways and paths of the *baal ha-yahrzeit*), and consequently all the elevations of the *yahrzeit* are "performed" *by them*—*they take the lead* in all the revelations that are made above, through which there is also made below an addition of light in the greatest abundance, and first and foremost—regarding us in particular—an addition of strength and the highest assistance in the service of each and every one in the ways and paths of the *baal ha-yahrzeit*.

**9.** And among the main matters in this:

The service of the Alter Rebbe was primarily—as the Rebbe Rayatz said in several *sichos*—to reveal the path of Chassidus Chabad, and not to be satisfied with that, but also to spread the path of Chassidus Chabad. And as is known, the Alter Rebbe wanted the teachings of Chassidus Chabad to belong (not only to individuals of stature, and not only to a special type of Jew, but) to every Jew.

The Alter Rebbe engaged in this himself, and our Rebbes, his successors, engaged in this, and they handed it over to us and commanded us to engage in this—in order to *bestow the merit* upon us in this.

The Rebbe Rayatz said regarding the writing of the *Sefer Torah* for the welcoming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, that it was in his power to write the *Sefer Torah* himself, but he wanted to *bestow the merit of this upon all of Israel*, and therefore he gave the ability and the possibility that everyone could participate in this.

And so it is regarding the engagement in spreading the wellsprings outward in order to bring about the coming of Mashiach ("When will the Master come? When your wellsprings spread outward")—that our Rebbes could have brought this about themselves in the manner of "a *tzaddik* decrees and Hashem fulfills," but their desire was to *bestow the merit upon each one of us* that we too should have a connection and participation in the action of bringing Mashiach ("bringing Mashiach down") here below ten *tefachim*, and therefore they left us a place so that we too, from our side, could do something in spreading the wellsprings outward. For when we have a share in the preparation and introduction to the coming of Mashiach ("your wellsprings will spread outward"), we will also have a share—not in the manner of "bread of shame"—in the coming of Mashiach ("the Master will come"), speedily in our days.

**10.** And in this matter too, the Alter Rebbe showed the way—in what manner the action of spreading the wellsprings outward must be done:

The Rebbe Rayatz told in several *sichos* about the way the Alter Rebbe acted in spreading the wellsprings outward—that upon arriving in any city, he would enter the *beis medrash* or the *shul*, stand and say a matter in the *revealed* Torah, and after he would "capture" the audience of learners ("when he would capture the audience")—or confuse them... (in each place according to its matter)—through his words in the revealed Torah, he would begin to say a matter from the teachings of Chassidus, and thereby he would transform them from one essence to another!

And this way the Alter Rebbe showed also to us,

—and not only that, but after he opened and paved the way, our work in this is incomparably easier, and all the more so since we are promised that this work will certainly be successful—

that when we meet a Jew who for the time being is not a Chassid, we must "capture" him ("capture him") through the *revealed Torah*, and when we confuse him or break his reality through this, then he becomes a vessel for the teachings of Chassidus, and we can transform him from one essence to another.

Chassidim in general, and *Temimim* in particular, from whom the Rebbes demanded especially to be "candles to illuminate," must go and light the candles, "the candle of Hashem is the soul of man," of those Jews whose candle is not currently burning and illuminating within them, and it goes without saying that it is not illuminating outside of them—after each one precedes and lights his own candle first, and through the "fire" within him lights also the candles of other Jews. But, in order for that Jew (whose candle we must light) to allow us to approach him—we must "capture him" in the way the Alter Rebbe showed—through the revealed Torah, and through this he will certainly succeed, and afterwards he will also make him a Chassid. However, for this, one needs "weapons"... and not only the teachings of Chassidus, but also the revealed Torah.

And since each one of us has been made a "shooter" (archer)—as the expression that was common with the Rebbe Rayatz: "Each one of us has been made into a shooter"—we have no choice but to take the rifle and shoot, and presumably the shot will be toward the correct target ("one will hit where one needs to shoot").

—(The Rebbe smiled and said:) There is a story about someone who said that he knows how to shoot, but he does not know (since they forgot to teach him) how one must hold the rifle, from this side or from the other side... but regarding our matter: since "there is a presumption that a colleague does not produce from his hand something that is not fixed," then, when they gave us rifles, presumably they gave us rifles such that we can shoot only in the correct direction!

We only need to load the rifle with a "bullet" of the revealed Torah, and through this we nullify the other from his reality, until we transform him from one essence to another, as mentioned above.

**11.** And this is not coming for a sermon, but the intent is regarding actual practice:

One must add strength and extra effort in the study of the revealed Torah, for, in addition to the greatness of the matter of fulfilling a *mitzvah*, and especially the *mitzvah* of Torah study in its own right, we are also promised that the study of the revealed Torah will be a great assistance in our mission in this world—spreading the wellsprings outward—that it will give us a special approach, and a special qualification and preparation for the fulfillment of this mission, so that speedily in our days we will be able to see in every place and corner ("wherever one turns") that a "Chassid *yid*" (who walks as a Chassid) in a way that another reality does not take up place at all, like the well-known story-proverb, meaning, that in every place and in every corner ("wherever one turns and wherever one directs oneself") there will be *Elokus* in revelation, as it is written, "The earth will be full of the knowledge of Hashem."

And this matter is done through the light in the Torah, this is the teachings of Chassidus, the soul of Torah, and with the introduction of the "body" and the "vessel"—broad vessels—broad and great knowledge in the revealed Torah, each one according to his value, standing, and situation. And then the desire of the *baal ha-yahrzeit* is fulfilled that there should be the unification of the revealed and Chassidus together, and in a way that we see the action of the teachings of Chassidus also in the revealed Torah—as the Rebbe Rayatz explains in the *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus* that there are two matters in the teachings of Chassidus: (a) through it one receives knowledge in the order of *hishtalshelus* and knowledge of the Creator, (b) through it one receives a different view ("a different look"), a different understanding and grasp, and a completely different vitality in the revealed Torah. And for this (for matter b) there is a need for "material" (substances)—the revealed Torah—in which there will be the action of the teachings of Chassidus to add vitality, etc.

And in order to fulfill the desire and the will and the yearning of the *baal ha-yahrzeit*—there is a need for all those who are demanded to be "candles to illuminate" to be able to leave their four cubits and travel throughout the world and confuse and shake up the world through the *revealed* Torah, and then they will say: "See what has come," and they will sanctify them through the hidden Torah, and thereby make them "lively and happy Jews," in the two lights in the Torah, the light of the revealed and the light of the hidden.

***

**12.** It is known the story that the Rebbe Rayatz told about the order that the Maggid established with the Alter Rebbe at the beginning of his arrival in Mezritch, that his son (R' Avraham) the "Malach" would study with the Alter Rebbe the teachings of Chassidus (the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the Maggid), and the Alter Rebbe would study with the "Malach" the revealed Torah. And when they began to study the beginning of the *Shas*, "From what time do we recite the *Shema* in the evenings," and the Alter Rebbe began to explain the *Mishnah* according to the revealed, the "Malach" said that he explains "from what time" (*mei'eimatai*) from the language of awe and fear, etc.

And one must explain the lesson and instruction from this story, for all the stories that they told us, we can and must derive from them a lesson and instruction in matters belonging to us.

—Not long ago I received a letter from someone, and in it he writes to me that it is found in the books that stories of *tzaddikim* are in the category of "Maaseh Merkavah."

(The Rebbe smiled and said:) I have not found this proverb in the books, and therefore I leave this on the responsibility of the aforementioned... but, what is certainly clear is that in stories of *tzaddikim* there is an intent and purpose, and especially a story that one hears from a *tzaddik*, and in particular—from a *Nasi*, whose entire essence and matter is to lead his flock, when a *Nasi* tells a story (like the aforementioned story), it is certainly a matter belonging to us that we can and must learn the instruction in it, as follows.

**13.** And first and foremost—the lesson and instruction from the joining and connection of the Alter Rebbe and the Malach to study together, a joining and connection of two Jews in the study of Torah:

One Jew by himself—is not a complete reality, but rather, a reality such that he "is fit to be joined" with another Jew, who, through their joining together, there is made (not only an addition in quantity, but also) a change in quality, from one extreme to the other.

And proof of this—from that which we find in the Midrash regarding the Giving of the Torah, that "if Israel were missing even one person, etc.":

The Giving of the Torah is the most elevated matter—the purpose of the intent of the creation of all the worlds, since in the Giving of the Torah there was the nullification of the decree, the nullification of the cutting ("the cut") and the separation between the upper and lower realms ("the upper realms would not descend to the lower realms and the lower realms would not ascend to the upper realms"), and a connection was made between the upper and lower realms ("the lower realms will ascend to the upper realms and the upper realms will descend to the lower realms").

And all this depends on the joining of one Jew, whoever he may be, to the totality of Israel, for "if Israel were missing even one person, etc.," and only through the joining of that one is the totality of the matter of the Giving of the Torah made possible.

And from this it is also understood the greatness of the elevation that is made through the connection and joining of one Jew to a general matter of Torah and *mitzvos* [and all matters of Torah and *mitzvos* are general matters: regarding *mitzvos*, every *mitzvah* is included in all the *mitzvos*, as explained in the *maamarim* of Chassidus that the reason for the fact that "one who is engaged in a *mitzvah* is exempt from a *mitzvah*" is because in the *mitzvah* that he is engaged in, the *mitzvah* that he is exempt from is also included; and all the more so regarding Torah, which is above time and place, unlike *mitzvos* which have the division of time and place, like the division of the 248 limbs and 365 sinews (which are against the 248 positive *mitzvos* and 365 negative *mitzvos*), unlike Torah which is like the blood that goes and circulates in all the limbs equally]—that this is not an addition in quantity only, but a change and great elevation in quality.

**14.** And in order that the connection and joining should be *true*—this is through the introduction of "From what time do we recite the *Shema* in the evenings," "from what time" (*mei'eimatai*) from the language of awe and fear (according to the interpretation of the "Malach"), which is the matter of acceptance of the yoke:

A joining and connection—can be in a way that it is only toward the outside, while inside the status and situation of separation remains, and nevertheless it is considered a connection. And as we find in the *Mishnah* differences in laws in the manners of joining and connection regarding ritual impurity and purity. But, the intent is that there should be a joining and connection both from the outside and from the inside, etc., a true joining and connection, and even truly to the truth.

And more specifically:

When the connection of one Jew with his fellow is from ulterior motives, physical motives, or even spiritual motives—this is not a true connection, for his intent is not to the connection itself, but to the profit and benefit in the physical or spiritual as a result of the connection.

And for example: when several Jews join for a *minyan* so that they will have the merit to say a matter of holiness, knowing the greatness of the elevation that is in the matter—this is indeed a connection, and a connection in a matter of Torah and *mitzvos*, but, if the intent of the connection is only from this benefit—which is indeed a benefit in holiness, that an elevation will be added in his soul, in his spirit, and in his *nefesh*, but nevertheless only a private benefit—this is a connection from an ulterior motive, and is not a true connection, truly to the truth.

A true connection is (not from any ulterior motive and benefit, but) from the *truth of the matter*—as the Alter Rebbe explains in *Tanya* that "the *nefesh* and the *ruach*—who knows their greatness and their elevation in their root and their source in the Living God, since they are all compatible and one Father for all of them... from the side of the root of their *nefesh* in the One Hashem," and through this is made "Bless us, our Father, all of us as one in the light of Your face," "Your face" specifically, the inwardness and essence of the *Ein Sof* *Baruch Hu*.

And to add, that this connection which is "from the side of the root of their *nefesh* in the One Hashem," is above the totality of Torah and *mitzvos*, for the root of the souls of Israel is above the root of Torah and *mitzvos*, as our Sages said, "The thought of Israel preceded everything," even the thought of Torah, for in the Torah itself it is said "Command the children of Israel," "Speak to the children of Israel," and from this is proof that "Israel preceded."

And such a connection is demanded from a Jew while he is below in this physical world—in which he must complete the supreme intent to be for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower realms, through the revelation and continuation of the "essence of the *Shechinah*" (which was in the lower realms), above the level of the "*Shechinah*" as it is in all the worlds, even in the world of *Atzilus* and in the worlds of the *Ein Sof* that are before *Atzilus*—that also below in this physical world his connection with his fellow should be (not from the benefit that is in the matter, even a benefit of holiness, but) "from the side of the root of their *nefesh* in the One Hashem," which is above Torah and *mitzvos*.

And since this connection is above the totality of the matter of Torah and *mitzvos*, the way to come to this is through *acceptance of the yoke* specifically. And this is the hint and instruction from the continuation of the story about the study of the Alter Rebbe and the Malach, that the Malach explained "from what time" from the language of awe and fear, a matter of acceptance of the yoke, which is also the content of "we recite the *Shema* in the evenings," "he should accept upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven first."

**15.** And this matter constitutes the beginning of the study of the Oral Torah, and in a way that the study is both in the revealed Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus (the interpretation of the Malach in the words of the *Mishnah*) together:

The matter of the Oral Torah—as the Alter Rebbe explains in *Iggeres HaKodesh* in the interpretation of the statement at the conclusion of the *Shas* "Whoever studies *halachos* every day, etc."—is that in it is revealed the Supreme Will, may He be blessed, which is clothed in the 613 *mitzvos* of the Torah, to know the action that they should do, how to conduct oneself in thought, speech, and action in actual practice in the day-to-day life in this physical world.

And the general point of His will, may He be blessed, from each one of Israel—is that the connection of Israel with Hashem should be through the Torah both in the revealed and in the hidden, as the statement "Three bonds are bound one to the other, Israel, Torah, and Hashem, and all of them are hidden and revealed,"

And in two ways: (a) the bond of the "hidden" of Hashem, Torah, and Israel between them, and the bond of the "revealed" of Hashem, Torah, and Israel between them, (b) the bond of the hidden of Hashem with the revealed of Hashem, the revealed of Hashem with the hidden of Torah, the hidden of Torah with the revealed of Torah, the revealed of Torah with the hidden of Israel, and the hidden of Israel with the revealed of Israel,

And in every way—in the "revealed" of Israel, while they are in this physical world, the "hidden" of Hashem, the essence and being of the *Ein Sof* *Baruch Hu*, is also continued and revealed.

And all this is continued and revealed in this physical and material world, that in it is made the revelation of "Hashem is One and His Name is One," "When I am written I am read" (unlike in this time that *Havayah* is written and *Adnut* is read), and up to the revelation of the *power of the essence* that is in the creation of something from nothing, as the Alter Rebbe explains in *Iggeres HaKodesh* that "the being and essence of the Emanator, may He be blessed, whose existence is from His essence and is not caused by any cause that preceded Him, *chas v'shalom*... He alone has the power and ability to create something from nothing and absolute nothingness, without any other cause and reason preceding this 'something'."

And so it will be for us—through the service of the connection of hidden and revealed [in the path of the Alter Rebbe who opened and paved for each one of us, and showed not only that we can walk in it, but also how to walk in it, so that this is in the power of each one of us], that each one will connect the hidden and revealed within him (in Israel), through this there will be for him the connection of hidden and revealed in the Torah, for then the connection of hidden and revealed of Hashem also acts, and consequently, also the hidden end, "the heart to the mouth is not revealed," is continued and revealed below ten *tefachim*, and we merit the complete and true Redemption speedily in our days.

***

**16.** It was discussed several times about the need for reviewing Chassidus in *shuls*.

And the reason for this is because of the benefit that is in the matter—and in two: (a) for the *bochurim* themselves, that in order to review Chassidus by heart, they will need by necessity to study Chassidus themselves (for it is impossible to review without studying beforehand...). (b) for the *baalei-batim* who are in the *shuls*.

And now, regarding the first benefit, the study of Chassidus and the knowledge of Chassidus—there are those among the *yungeleit* (young married men) and all the more so the *baalei-batim* who are already "advanced in years" who think that they do not need this benefit, since the teachings of Chassidus are for them "as if placed in a box"... and they only need to "air out" the matters from time to time, a matter that is not involved with effort at all,

But, to *exert* themselves to study the *maamar* by heart, and afterwards to go to *shul* and review it—they are not

---

**Hebrew:**

## בס"ד. ש"פ וארא, כ"ח טבת, מבה"ח שבט, ה'תשי"ב

### בס"ד. ש"פ וארא, כ"ח טבת, מבה"ח שבט, ה'תשי"ב

(הנחה בלתי מוגה)
וידבר[ftnref\_1398\_1] אלקים אל משה ויאמר אליו אני הוי' וארא אל אברהם גו' בא-ל שדי ושמי הוי' לא נודעתי להם גו'[ftnref\_1399\_2], ובהמשך הכתובים נאמר[ftnref\_1400\_3] והוצאתי גו' והצלתי גו' וגאלתי גו' ולקחתי גו', ד' לשונות של גאולה, וידעתם כי אני הוי'. ומשמעות הענין, דע"י הגאולה ממצרים דוקא באו לידיעת שם הוי'. וצריך להבין, דהרי גם אצל האבות מצינו ענין גילוי שם הוי', כמ"ש וירא הוי' אל אברם[ftnref\_1401\_4], וירא אליו הוי'[ftnref\_1402\_5], וכיו"ב. וא"כ מהו ושמי הוי' לא נודעתי להם. גם צריך להבין מדוע זכו למדריגה זו דוקא ע"י יציאת ממצרים, הגאולה ממצרים. דמשמע מזה, שדוקא ע"י שהיו בגלות מצרים ונגאלו ממנו עי"ז זכו לגילוי שם הוי'. דאי אפשר לומר שגילוי שם הוי' הוא רק משום שאינם בגלות מצרים, שהרי גם האבות לא היו בגלות, ומ"מ ושמי הוי' לא נודעתי להם. ומוכח מזה דכוונת הכתוב, שדוקא ע"י שהיו בגלות מצרים ונגאלו ממנו, עי"ז באו לגילוי דוידעתם כי אני הוי'. וצריך להבין הענין בזה.
ויובן כל זה[ftnref\_1403\_6] בהקדם מארז"ל[ftnref\_1404\_7] אם ישראל עושין תשובה נגאלין ואם לאו אין נגאלין, ומשמע מזה[ftnref\_1405\_8] שהתשובה אינה רק אם יש חטא ועון אלא בכל אופן אי אפשר שתהא הגאולה ללא תשובה. וכן פסק הרמב"ם[ftnref\_1406\_9] דאין ישראל נגאלין אלא בתשובה, דלשון אין כו' אלא הואלעיכובא[ftnref\_1407\_10]. וצריך להבין, מהו ההכרח שלפני הגאולה יהי' ענין התשובה. דבשלמא אם יש חטא ועון מובן מדוע צ"ל תשובה ע"ז לפני הגאולה דלעתיד, שהרי לע"ל כתיב[ftnref\_1408\_11] ואת רוח הטומאה אעביר מן הארץ, ולכן צ"ל לפני זה ביטול החטאים והעוונות, שלא תהי' לעניני לעו"ז שום אחיזה אצל האדם במחדו"מ שלו. אבל כשאין חטאים למה צריך לענין התשובה.
אך הענין הוא[ftnref\_1409\_12], דהנה בנוגע לענין התשובה (שעתידים ישראל לעשות בסוף גלותן[ftnref\_1406\_9]) כתיב[ftnref\_1410\_13] כי לא ידח ממנו נידח, ממנו דייקא, דקאי על עצומ"ה ית', שכל הניצוצות שבכל נפשות ישראל סופן לאשתאבא בגופא דמלכא[ftnref\_1411\_14], עצומ"ה ית'. אך איך תהי' הנפש הזאת שהיא בבחינת גבול ונברא משתאבת בגופא דמלכא, עצומ"ה א"ס ב"ה, שהוא בחינת בלי גבול ובורא. ויתר על כן, דבאמת אי אפשר לומר עליו ח"ו גם התואר בלי גבול[ftnref\_1412\_15], כשם שאי אפשר לומר ח"ו שהוא בגדר גבול, דעצומ"ה הוא שלילת הגבול ושלילת הבל"ג, שלילת החיוב ושלילת השלילה[ftnref\_1413\_16]. וא"כ יפלא ביותר איך תהי' התקשרות הנפש עם העצמות, שהנפש היא בבחינת גבול בקצה השני ממש, ובפרט כשהיא מלובשת בגוף. אך הענין הוא, דההתקשרות היא ע"י תורה ומצוות. דהתורה היא חכמתו ורצונו של הקב"ה[ftnref\_1414\_17] והמצוות הן איברין דמלכא[ftnref\_1415\_18], ואעפ"כ נשתלשלו וירדו ממקום כבודם ומתלבשים בענינים גשמיים. דלענין התורה הרי ארז"ל[ftnref\_1416\_19] דכשבקשו המלאכים שתינתן להם התורה הי' המענה על בקשתם כלום למצרים ירדתם, יצה"ר יש ביניכם וכו'. דמזה שענין זה הובא לגבי נתינת התורה (ולא רק קיום המצוות) מוכח שהתורה עצמה נתלבשה בדברים גשמיים. וכן הוא גם במצוות בפשטות, שהמצוות הם בדברים גשמיים. ואפילו המצוות שקיומם הוא במוח ובלב, הרי שיעור המצוה הוא שתהא נרגשת במוח הגשמי ובלב הגשמי[ftnref\_1417\_20]. ולכן התומ"צ הם הממוצעיםהמקשרים ומחברים את הנפש האלקית שהיא בגדר גבול ומקום ומלובשת בגוף, שתוכל להבטל ולהכלל באור א"ס ב"ה, לאשתאבא בגופא דמלכא, עצומ"ה ית'. ומטעם זה נקראו המצוות בשם לבושים[ftnref\_1418\_21], שהם מלבישים את נשמת האדם שתוכל להכלל באור א"ס ולחזות בנועם הוי'[ftnref\_1419\_22] ולאשתאבא בגופא דמלכא.
וזהו[ftnref\_1420\_23] מ"ש[ftnref\_1421\_24] ואברהם זקן בא בימים גו', ואיתא בזוהר[ftnref\_1422\_25] על הפסוק, דבא בימים פירושו ביומין שלמים, אינון יומין עילאין שהם הלבושים דתומ"צ. דהימים הם בחינת לבושים להלביש את נשמת האדם, והם הם לבושי התומ"צ, שעל ידם יוכל האדם להמשיך עליו אחדותו ית'. וזהו מ"ש ואברהם זקן בא בימים, זקן זה שקנה חכמה[ftnref\_1423\_26], דבחינת חכמה הוא גילוי האחדות דלמעלה, כמבואר בתניא[ftnref\_1424\_27] דבחינת החכמה היא מה שהוא לבדו הוא ואין זולתו, וכדי להגיע למדריגה זו הי' אברהם בא בימים, היינו לבושי התומ"צ. וענין זה קשור עם ימים כפשוטם, שכל יום צריך להיות מלא בקיום התומ"צ, כמאמר[ftnref\_1425\_28] בכל יומא ויומא עביד עבידתי', היינו שבכל יום ויום צ"ל קיום התומ"צ שבאותו היום. דעי"ז אפשר להגיע להתקשרות הנפש עם עצומ"ה ית'. ולכן צריך האדם לסגל תורה ומצוות ואפילו מצוה אחת כמה פעמים כמספר הימים אשר ניתנו לו מן השמים. ועוד זאת, שלפעמים עושה מצוה אחת כמה פעמים באותו היום, וכמו בענין התפלות שיש ג' תפלות בכל יום ובשבת ויו"ט ד' תפלות וביו"כ ה' תפלות. ויש להוסיף בזה, דהנה לכאורה אינו מובן, דהרי ידוע שמעלת הנשמות היא היותן בבחינת מהלכים דוקא, שעבודתם היא בבחינת הילוך ועלי' ממדריגה למדריגה, וכמבואר[ftnref\_1426\_29] בפירוש הכתוב[ftnref\_1427\_30] ונתתי לך מהלכים בין העומדים האלה, וא"כ מדוע צ"ל העסק באותה מצוה כמה פעמים באותו היום. אך ע"פ הנ"ל מובן, דהן אמת שהעבודה עצמה היא בבחינת עלי' מדרגא לדרגא, אבל המצוות הם רק בבחינתלבושים שעל ידם יוכל לקשר נפשו באלקות, ולכן צ"ל עשיית מצוות אלו פעמים רבות כדי שתוכל נשמתו להתקשר עם אלקות, ואז תוכל להיות העלי' וההילוך.
ובזה[ftnref\_1428\_31] יש לבאר[ftnref\_1429\_32] מה שמצינו סתירה בענין החיוב דתלמוד תורה, דבמ"א ארז"ל[ftnref\_1430\_33] דמי שאפשר לו לעסוק בתורה ואינו עוסק עליו נאמר[ftnref\_1431\_34] כי דבר הוי' בזה גו' הכרת תכרת גו', ובמ"א אמרו[ftnref\_1432\_35] דמי שאי אפשר לו לעסוק בתורה כל היום מפני עסקו במשא ומתן די לו בפרק אחד שחרית ופרק אחד ערבית. דאי נימא דזה שהמתבטל מת"ת עליו נאמר כי דבר הוי' בזה הוא מצד מעלת התורה, שהוא בזיון התורה, אם כן מדוע בעל עסק די לו בפ"א שחרית ופרק א' ערבית. ואם נאמר שענין עסק התורה תלוי בפנאי שיש לאדם, דלכן מי שהוא בעל עסק די לו בפ"א שחרית ופ"א ערבית, א"כ מה הרעש אם מי שיש לו פנאי מתבטל שעה קלה, עד שעליו נאמר הכרת תכרת גו'. אך הענין מובן ע"פ משנת"ל שהתורה היא לבוש לנשמה שתוכל להתקשר עם אלקות, לאשתאבא בגופא דמלכא. ולכן ה"ז תלוי באיזו נשמה מדובר. דיש נשמה שצריכה יותר ללבושים, ויש נשמה שאצלה הצורך בלבושים אינו גדול כ"כ. ולכן מי שאי אפשר לו לעסוק בתורה כל היום כולו מחמת עסק הפרנסה, הרי מאחר שלא הזמינו לו פרנסתו מן השמים שיהי' פנוי כל היום לעסוק בתורה, מוכח מזה שנשמתו אינה צריכה כ"כ ללבושי התורה, ודי לו בפ"א שחרית ופ"א ערבית. אך מי שאפשר לו לעסוק בתורה כל היום, מוכח מזה שנשמתו צריכה ליותר לבושים, ולכן אסור לו לבטל אפילו רגע א', אלא צריך לעסוק כל היום כפי שיעור הלבושים הדרושים לשורש נשמתו, ואם לאו הרי הכרת תכרת גו', שאין נשמתו יכולה לעלות וליראות באור ה'. וראי' לדבר ממה שארז"ל[ftnref\_1433\_36] שמי שביטל מצות ק"ש אפילו פעם אחת כאילו לא קרא כל ימיו, דמכיון שחסר לו בלבוש זה, א"כ חסר אצלו בהתקשרות עם עצומ"ה א"ס ב"ה. ודוקא ע"י קיום התומ"צ בכל יום ויום, כפי מספר הימים הקצובים לו, אפשר שתהי' התקשרות הנשמות עם עצומ"ה א"ס ב"ה.ומבאר רבינו הזקן[ftnref\_1434\_37], דהנה אין כל אדם זוכה לזה שיהיו כל ימיו שלימים ולא יחסר מהם אפי' שעה אחת רגע א'. ויש לומר בביאור דיוק לשון רבינו הזקן שאין כל אדם זוכה לזה, דמשמע שזהו ענין של זכות מלמעלה, ולא דבר התלוי בבחירה. וי"ל דמובן הוא ע"פ הידוע[ftnref\_1435\_38] דביטול תורה אין אדם ניצול ממנו בכל יום, כמובן ממארז"ל[ftnref\_1436\_39] ג' עבירות אין אדם ניצול מהם בכל יום כו', ונמצא שאין זה דבר התלוי בבחירת האדם אלא צריך לזה זכות וסייעתא דשמיא. וממשיך רבינו הזקן[ftnref\_1434\_37], דהעצה לזה היא שיהי' כל ימיו בתשובה[ftnref\_1437\_40]. פירוש הדברים, דכיון שאין כל אדם יכול לזכות לזה שלא יהי' חסרון בלבושו, וא"כ איך יבוא האדם להתקשרות נשמתו עם עצומ"ה א"ס ב"ה, הנה העצה לזה היא ע"י התשובה. דגם ע"י תשובה יכול לבוא לאשתאבא בגופא דמלכא. ומבאר שם, דשובה אותיות בושה, וכן תשוב אותיות בושת. דענין תשובה הוא שיבוא ליראה בושת, יראה מחמת בושה. דע"י שיעמיק בשכלו בגדולת ה' אשר הוא ממכ"ע וסוכ"ע וכולא קמי' כל"ח, ואור אין סוף למעלה עד אין קץ ולמטה עד אין תכלית[ftnref\_1438\_41], בודאי תיפול עליו הבושה ממנו ית'[ftnref\_1439\_42]. דאף שהוא אוהב את השם וירא את השם, מ"מ אין האהוי"ר שלו נחשבת לכלום. וכמו שמביא ע"ז אדמו"ר הצ"צ[ftnref\_1440\_43] מ"ש רבינו הזקן בד"ה וטהר לבנו[ftnref\_1441\_44] בשם הרב המגיד נ"ע[ftnref\_1442\_45], דפירוש יראה בושת הוא ע"ד מ"ש[ftnref\_1443\_46] כתר עליון אף על גב דאיהו אור צח אור מצוחצח אוכם הוא קדם עילות העילות. וכאשר האדם ידקדק על עצמו וישים אל ליבו איך אפילו כתר עליון דאצילות אוכם הוא ומתבייש נגד אוא"ס ב"ה, אז תיפול עליו אימה ופחד ביותר. ובפרט כשיתבונן האדם שהוא אינו יודע גם מהות הע"ס, שהרי ידיעתו בהם היא רק ידיעת המציאות ולא השגת המהות, וכ"ש וק"ו שאינו יודע בחינת כתרא עילאה, ובפרט כמו שהוא לפני הצמצום, דגם כתרא עלאה שלפני הצמצום אוכם הוא קדם עילת העילות.[דענין זה הוא בכל המדריגות שבכתרא עילאה, דאפילו במדריגות הכי עליונות שבו, ואפילו במדריגה שלמעלה מגדר מדריגות כלל, גם שם אוכם הוא קדם עילת העילות, דאדרבה, עילת העילות נמצא למטה דוקא, כמבואר במ"א[ftnref\_1444\_47]]. וע"י התבוננות זו בא האדם לבחינת בושה, שזהו ענין התשובה. וע"י התשובה תוכל להיות התקשרות הנפש בעצומ"ה א"ס ב"ה.
וביאור הענין הוא[ftnref\_1445\_48], דהנה כתיב[ftnref\_1446\_49] כי נער ישראל ואוהבהו וממצרים קראתי לבני. הענין הוא כמו שאנו רואים עד"מ אצל בן נער, שכל זמן שנמצא בקירוב לאביו ואביו מראה לו אהבתו ומקרבהו באהבה וחיבה יתירה, אז מתרהב הבן בנפשו לעשות מילין דשטותא מצד קטנות המוחין, אף שהוא נגד רצון אביו, ואף אם אביו מוחה בידו אינו משגיח בו ואינו שומע לקולו. ורק כשאביו מסתיר פניו ממנו ודוחה אותו החוצה עד שאומר לו שאינו אביו כלל, אז דוקא יתעורר הבן להיות בקרבת אביו. וכך הוא הענין באהבת ישראל למקום ב"ה המסותרת בלב כל או"א מישראל, שאינה יוצאת מן ההעלם אל הגילוי כי אם ע"י ההתבוננות בריחוקו מה'. וזהו כי נער ישראל ואוהבהו, דכאשר ישנו ענין הקירוב (ואוהבהו) יכול להיות נער ישראל, שיעשה מעשי נערות וקטנות, ודוקא ממצרים קראתי לבני, דע"י מצרים הוא מיצר וקטנות, ענין הבושה הנ"ל, עי"ז קראתי לבני, שעי"ז הוא גילוי האהבה ביתר שאת.
והנה בפרטיות יותר ענין גלות מצרים שעל ידו הוא גילוי האהבה ה"ז מה שהאדם נמצא בעבודתו במצב של ירידה, שזה מעורר בו עוד יותר את הרגש הבושה והתשובה. ובזה גופא יש כמה מדריגות, וכמבואר במאמר אדמו"ר הזקן[ftnref\_1447\_50] שיש בחינת מצרים דקדושה ובחינת מצרים דלעו"ז. דבחינת מצרים דקדושה הוא שמסתפק בתורתו ועבודתו שלומד בתורה ועובד ה', ואינו משתדל להרבות בתורה ומע"ט אלא די לו במה שעוסק, כי לפי ראות עיניו יוצא ידי חובתו. ויש לומר שזהו גם ענין קיום המצוות כמצות אנשים מלומדה[ftnref\_1448\_51]. ומבחינת מצרים שבקדושה נמשךונשתלשל עד שנעשה למטה בקליפה בחינת מצרים דלעו"ז, דהיינו בחינת פגם הברית. דלפעמים הוא שלא ברצונו, שמטמאין אותו בע"כ שלא ברצונו במקרה לילה, וכמ"ש[ftnref\_1449\_52] אשר מצרים מעבידים אותם. וענין יציאת מצרים הוא בחינת תשובה על ידי ענין זה עצמו, כשרואה בעצמו שהוא רחוק מה' בתכלית, דאז ממצרים קראתי לבני, שהריחוק דוקא מעורר בו את התשובה ואת ההרגש שהוא בני, ועי"ז מקשר נפשו עם עצומ"ה, לאשתאבא בגופא דמלכא.
ומכל זה יובן במעלת ענין התשובה[ftnref\_1450\_53], דגם מי שאין ימיו שלמים, שחסר בלבושי התומ"צ שלו, דאין כל אדם זוכה לזה כנ"ל, אפשר שתהי' התקשרות נפשו בעצומ"ה ע"י התשובה. ואדרבה, יש מעלה בהתקשרות שע"י התשובה על ההתקשרות שע"י לבושי התומ"צ. דההמשכה שע"י לבושי התומ"צ היא בבחינת גבול, מבחינת ממכ"ע. אבל ע"י התשובה, שהתשובה היא בשעתא חדא וברגעא חדא[ftnref\_1451\_54], הרי ההמשכה שעי"ז היא בלי גבול. וכמשנת"ל דענין התשובה היא הבושה, שכל ענין של מדידה והגבלה יודע שהוא אוכם קדם עילת העילות, ורוצה לצאת מהגבלה זו, ולכן ההמשכה שע"י התשובה, בחינת ממצרים קראתי לבני, היא המשכה נעלית עוד יותר.
וזהו[ftnref\_1452\_55] וארא אל אברהם אל יצחק ואל יעקב בא-ל שדי גו', דהגילוי לאבות הוא בחינת א-ל שדי, דבכללות זהו ענין ממכ"ע. דהגם שיש כמה בחינות בא-ל שדי[ftnref\_1453\_56], דישנו ענין שאמר לעולמו די[ftnref\_1454\_57], שזהו טבע העולם שהוא בבחינת העלם והסתר, ויש ענין א-ל שדי למעלה מזה, דע"ז כתיב[ftnref\_1455\_58] והריקותי לכם ברכה עד בלי די וארז"ל[ftnref\_1456\_59] כדי סיפוקו[ftnref\_1457\_60], שהיא המשכת אלקות בעולמות, מ"מ ה"ז רק כדי סיפוקו ולא ענין העשירות. וכידוע[ftnref\_1458\_61] בענין די מחסורו אשר יחסר לו[ftnref\_1459\_62] אפילו סוס לרכובעליו ועבד לרוץ לפניו[ftnref\_1460\_63], שכל זה הוא ענין של מילוי החסרון בלבד ולא ענין של עשירות ומותרות. דהיינו ההמשכה שמבחינת ממכ"ע. אמנם ע"י הירידה לגלות מצרים דוקא הגיעו לגילוי שם הוי', ממצרים קראתי לבני, ההמשכה מבחינת הוי', בלי גבול, וידעתם כי אני הוי'.
וזהו וידבר אלקים אל משה ויאמר אליו אני הוי'. דהנה פסוק זה הוא מענה[ftnref\_1461\_64] על שאלת משה לעיל למה הרעות לעם הזה[ftnref\_1462\_65], דהיינו למה הוצרך להיות כל ענין גלות מצרים. וע"ז בא המענה ויאמר אליו אני הוי', דתכלית ענין גלות מצרים הוא גילוי שם הוי'[ftnref\_1463\_66]. והגם[ftnref\_1464\_67] שהי' ענין שם הוי' גם אצל האבות כנ"ל, ה"ז בחינת הוי' דלתתא, בחינת שם הוי' השייך לעולמות, הוי' לשון מהווה[ftnref\_1465\_68]. אמנם ע"י הירידה דגלות מצרים באו לגילוי דוידעתם כי אני הוי' שלמעלה מגדרי העולם, דהוי' הוא הי' הווה ויהי' כאחד[ftnref\_1466\_69]. וענין זה בא ע"י עבודת התשובה כנ"ל, דזהו[ftnref\_1467\_70] מ"ש[ftnref\_1468\_71] ונתתי אותה לכם מורשה, כי האהבה הבאה מבחינת התשובה היא כמו ירושה שנפל לו הון רב אשר לא עמל בו, וכך האהבה וקרבת ה' הבאה ע"י התשובה והבושה היא שלא ע"י מעשיו הטובים דבר יום ביומו (כנ"ל) כי אם בשעה אחת, בתורת ירושה הבאה מלמעלה. ויש להוסיף עוד בזה, דענין הירושה הוא מצד שיש ליורש יחס אל המוריש ואינו נוגע בזה מצב היורש, ולכן גם חרש שוטה וקטן יורש[ftnref\_1469\_72], כי מה שנוגע הוא רק שיש לו יחס אל המוריש. וזהו מורשה אני הוי', דבכדי להגיע לבחינת הוי' דלעילא הוא ע"י ירושה. ועוד יש להוסיף, דמורשה הוא גם מלשון ראש, היינו ההתקשרות עם ראש העדה[ftnref\_1470\_73], ראשיכם שבטיכם, שע"י ההתקשרות עם ראשיכם שבטיכם[ftnref\_1471\_74] הנה גם חוטב עציך ושואב מימיך[ftnref\_1471\_74] יגיעו לגילוי שם הוי'. אך צ"ל ההתקשרות, ולא להפרד ח"ו מהמוריש והראש, וכנ"ל בענין התשובה, שהוא כמו הבן שאינו יכוללסבול שאביו אומר שאין הוא אביו, ורוצה להיות מקושר אליו. ועי"ז וידעתם כי אני הוי', שתהיו מקושרים (דעת לשון התקשרות[ftnref\_1472\_75]) לשם הוי' דלעילא, בחינת הי' הווה ויהי' כאחד, בחינת בל"ג, שכל זה בא ע"י התשובה.
------- \* -------

**English:**

## B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Va’era, 28 Teves, Mevarchim HaChodesh Shevat, 5712

(Unedited transcript)

"And Elokim spoke to Moshe and said to him, 'I am Hashem. And I appeared to Avraham, to Yitzchak, and to Yaakov as Kel Shaddai, but by My name Hashem I was not known to them.'" Further on in the verses, it is stated: "And I will take you out," "and I will rescue," "and I will redeem," "and I will take"—four expressions of redemption—"and you shall know that I am Hashem." The implication is that it was specifically through the redemption from Mitzrayim that they arrived at the knowledge of the name Hashem. 

We must understand this, for we find that the name Hashem was revealed to the Patriarchs as well, as it is written: "And Hashem appeared to Avram," "And Hashem appeared to him," and the like. If so, what is meant by "but by My name Hashem I was not known to them"? Furthermore, we must understand why they merited this level specifically through the exodus from Mitzrayim, the redemption from Mitzrayim. This implies that it was specifically because they were in the exile of Mitzrayim and were redeemed from it that they merited the revelation of the name Hashem. It is impossible to say that the revelation of the name Hashem is only because they were no longer in the exile of Mitzrayim, for the Patriarchs were also not in exile, yet "by My name Hashem I was not known to them." This proves that the intent of the verse is that specifically through having been in the exile of Mitzrayim and being redeemed from it, they arrived at the revelation of "and you shall know that I am Hashem." We must understand the concept here.

All of this can be understood by prefacing the teaching of our Sages: "If Yisrael repent, they are redeemed; and if not, they are not redeemed." This implies that teshuvah is not only necessary if there is sin and iniquity, but that in any case, it is impossible for the redemption to occur without teshuvah. The Rambam also rules that Yisrael are only redeemed through teshuvah, and the term "if not" implies a condition for the redemption. We must understand the necessity for teshuvah to precede the redemption. It is understandable that if there is sin and iniquity, teshuvah is required for them before the future redemption, for regarding the future it is written, "And I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," and therefore there must first be a nullification of sins and iniquities so that the *sitra achra* has no hold on a person in his thoughts, speech, and action. But when there are no sins, why is teshuvah necessary?

The matter is as follows: Regarding the teshuvah (which Yisrael are destined to perform at the end of their exile), it is written, "For no one cast away shall be cast away from Him"—"from Him" specifically, referring to the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, blessed be He, for all the sparks in all the souls of Yisrael will ultimately be drawn into the "Body of the King," the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, blessed be He. But how can this soul, which is in the category of a limited and created being, be drawn into the "Body of the King," the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, who is in the category of the Infinite and the Creator? Moreover, it is truly impossible to even apply the term "Infinite" to Him, just as it is impossible to say that He is in the category of "limited," for the *Atzmus* is the negation of limitation and the negation of the infinite, the negation of affirmation and the negation of negation. If so, it is all the more wondrous how the soul can be connected with the *Atzmus*, when the soul is in the category of limitation at the very opposite end, especially when it is clothed in a body.

The matter is that the connection is through Torah and mitzvos. The Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, blessed be He, and the mitzvos are the "limbs of the King." Nevertheless, they have descended and devolved from their place of glory and are clothed in physical matters. Regarding the Torah, our Sages said that when the angels requested that the Torah be given to them, the response to their request was, "Have you gone down to Mitzrayim? Is there an evil inclination among you?" The fact that this matter was raised regarding the giving of the Torah (and not only the performance of mitzvos) proves that the Torah itself was clothed in physical things. This is also true of the mitzvos in a simple sense, as the mitzvos are performed with physical objects. Even the mitzvos whose fulfillment is in the mind and heart, the measure of the mitzvah is that it be felt in the physical brain and physical heart. Therefore, Torah and mitzvos are the intermediaries that connect and unite the divine soul—which is in the category of limitation and space and is clothed in a body—so that it can be nullified and included in the light of the *Ein Sof*, to be drawn into the "Body of the King," the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, blessed be He. For this reason, the mitzvos are called "garments," as they clothe the soul of man so that it can be included in the light of the *Ein Sof* and "gaze upon the pleasantness of Hashem" and be drawn into the "Body of the King."

This is what is meant by "And Avraham was old, advanced in days," and it is stated in the Zohar on this verse that "advanced in days" means "complete days"—these are the supernal days, which are the garments of Torah and mitzvos. The days are the category of garments to clothe the soul of man, and they are the garments of Torah and mitzvos, through which a person can draw upon himself His unity. This is the meaning of "And Avraham was old, advanced in days"—"old" is one who has acquired wisdom, for the category of wisdom is the revelation of the unity from above, as explained in Tanya, that the category of wisdom is that "He alone is He, and there is nothing else." To reach this level, Avraham was "advanced in days," meaning the garments of Torah and mitzvos. This matter is connected to days in the literal sense, that every day must be filled with the performance of Torah and mitzvos, as the saying goes, "Every single day He performs His work," meaning that every day there must be the performance of the Torah and mitzvos of that day. Through this, it is possible to reach the connection of the soul with the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, blessed be He. Therefore, a person must accumulate Torah and mitzvos, even the same mitzvah many times, according to the number of days given to him from heaven. Furthermore, sometimes one performs the same mitzvah several times in one day, such as the prayers, where there are three prayers every day, four on Shabbos and Yom Tov, and five on Yom Kippur.

One might add: seemingly, this is difficult to understand, for it is known that the merit of the souls is that they are in the category of "walkers," whose service is in the category of movement and ascent from level to level, as explained in the interpretation of the verse, "And I will give you walkers among these who stand." If so, why is it necessary to engage in the same mitzvah several times in one day? But based on the above, it is understood: it is true that the service itself is in the category of ascent from level to level, but the mitzvos are only in the category of garments through which one can connect his soul to *Elokus*. Therefore, one must perform these mitzvos many times so that his soul can be connected with *Elokus*, and then the ascent and movement can take place.

With this, we can explain the contradiction we find regarding the obligation of Torah study. In one place, our Sages said that one who is able to engage in Torah and does not, of him it is said, "For he has despised the word of Hashem... he shall surely be cut off." In another place, they said that one who is unable to engage in Torah all day because of his business, it is sufficient for him to study one chapter in the morning and one chapter in the evening. If we say that the one who neglects Torah study is subject to "he shall surely be cut off" because of the greatness of the Torah—that it is a degradation of the Torah—then why is it sufficient for a businessman to study one chapter in the morning and one in the evening? And if we say that the matter of Torah study depends on the leisure time a person has, so that one who is a businessman is exempt with one chapter in the morning and one in the evening, then what is the outcry if someone who has leisure time neglects it for a short while, to the point that it is said of him "he shall surely be cut off"?

The matter is understood based on what was explained above, that the Torah is a garment for the soul so that it can connect with *Elokus*, to be drawn into the "Body of the King." Therefore, it depends on which soul is being discussed. There is a soul that needs more garments, and there is a soul for whom the need for garments is not as great. Therefore, one who is unable to engage in Torah all day long because of the business of earning a living—since his livelihood was not provided for him from heaven in a way that he would be free all day to engage in Torah—it is proven that his soul does not need the garments of Torah as much, and it is sufficient for him to study one chapter in the morning and one in the evening. But one who is able to engage in Torah all day, it is proven that his soul needs more garments, and therefore he is forbidden to neglect even one moment; rather, he must engage all day according to the measure of garments required for the root of his soul. If not, then "he shall surely be cut off," for his soul cannot ascend and gaze upon the light of Hashem. Proof of this is what our Sages said, that one who neglects the mitzvah of *Krias Shema* even once is as if he did not read it all his days, for since he lacks this garment, he lacks the connection with the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He. It is specifically through the performance of Torah and mitzvos every single day, according to the number of days allotted to him, that the connection of the souls with the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, can occur.

Our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains that not every person merits that all his days be complete, without missing even one hour or one moment. One can say in explanation of the precision of the Alter Rebbe's language, "not every person merits," that this implies it is a matter of merit from above, not something that depends on choice. It can be said that this is understood based on the well-known teaching that a person is not saved from *bitul Torah* (neglect of Torah) every day, as implied by our Sages' teaching that there are three sins from which a person is not saved every day. It turns out that this is not something that depends on a person's choice, but requires merit and heavenly assistance. The Alter Rebbe continues that the advice for this is that all his days should be in *teshuvah*. The meaning is: since not every person can merit that there be no deficiency in his garments, and if so, how can a person arrive at the connection of his soul with the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He? The advice for this is through *teshuvah*. For even through *teshuvah* one can come to be drawn into the "Body of the King."

He explains there that *shuvah* (repentance) shares the same letters as *boshah* (shame), and *teshuv* shares the same letters as *boshes* (shame). The concept of *teshuvah* is that one should arrive at "shame-fear," fear resulting from shame. By deepening his intellect in the greatness of Hashem—that He fills all worlds and encompasses all worlds, and everything is as nothing before Him, and the light of the *Ein Sof* is above without end and below without limit—shame before Him, blessed be He, will certainly fall upon him. For even though he loves Hashem and fears Hashem, his love and fear are considered as nothing. As the Tzemach Tzedek brings on this, what the Alter Rebbe wrote in the discourse *U'Taher Libenu* in the name of the Maggid: that the interpretation of "shame-fear" is like the teaching regarding the *Keser Elyon* (Supernal Crown), that even though it is "a bright light, a polished light," it is "black" before the Cause of all causes. When a person is precise with himself and takes to heart how even the *Keser Elyon* of *Atzilus* is "black" and is ashamed before the light of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, then awe and great fear will fall upon him. Especially when a person contemplates that he does not even know the essence of the *Sefiros*, for his knowledge of them is only knowledge of their existence and not the attainment of their essence—and all the more so, he does not know the category of *Keser Elyon*, especially as it is before the *Tzimtzum*, for even the *Keser Elyon* before the *Tzimtzum* is "black" before the Cause of all causes. (This matter applies to all levels within the *Keser Elyon*, for even in its most supernal levels, and even in the level that is above the category of levels entirely, even there it is "black" before the Cause of all causes; on the contrary, the Cause of all causes is found specifically below, as explained elsewhere). Through this contemplation, a person arrives at the category of shame, which is the concept of *teshuvah*. And through *teshuvah*, the connection of the soul with the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, can occur.

The explanation of the matter is as follows: It is written, "For Yisrael is a youth, and I loved him, and from Mitzrayim I called to My son." The matter is like what we see, for example, with a young boy: as long as he is in proximity to his father and his father shows him his love and draws him near with extra love and affection, the boy becomes emboldened in his soul to do foolish things due to the smallness of his intellect, even if it is against his father's will, and even if his father protests, he does not pay attention to him and does not listen to his voice. Only when his father hides his face from him and pushes him outside, to the point that he tells him he is not his father at all, then specifically the son is awakened to be in his father's proximity. Such is the matter of the love of Yisrael for the Omnipresent, blessed be He, which is hidden in the heart of every single one of Yisrael; it does not emerge from concealment to revelation except through the contemplation of his distance from Hashem. This is "For Yisrael is a youth, and I loved him"—when there is the matter of proximity ("and I loved him"), there can be "Yisrael is a youth," that he does deeds of youth and smallness. And specifically "from Mitzrayim I called to My son"—through Mitzrayim, which is constriction and smallness, the concept of shame mentioned above, through this "I called to My son," for through this is the revelation of love with greater intensity.

More specifically, the matter of the exile of Mitzrayim, through which the revelation of love occurs, is that a person finds himself in his service in a state of descent, which awakens in him even more the feeling of shame and *teshuvah*. Within this itself, there are several levels, as explained in the discourse of the Alter Rebbe, that there is a category of "Mitzrayim of holiness" and a category of "Mitzrayim of the *sitra achra*." The "Mitzrayim of holiness" is that he is satisfied with his Torah and service—he studies Torah and serves Hashem, but does not strive to increase in Torah and good deeds; rather, he is satisfied with what he is engaged in, because in his own eyes he has fulfilled his obligation. One could say that this is also the concept of performing mitzvos as "a commandment of men learned by rote." From the "Mitzrayim of holiness," it descends and devolves until it becomes below in the *kelipah* the category of "Mitzrayim of the *sitra achra*," which is the category of the blemish of the covenant. Sometimes it is against his will, that they defile him against his will through a nocturnal occurrence, as it is written, "which Mitzrayim enslave them." The concept of the exodus from Mitzrayim is the category of *teshuvah* through this very matter, when he sees in himself that he is distant from Hashem in the extreme, for then "from Mitzrayim I called to My son," for the distance specifically awakens in him *teshuvah* and the feeling that he is "My son," and through this he connects his soul with the *Atzmus*, to be drawn into the "Body of the King."

From all this, we can understand the merit of the matter of *teshuvah*: even one whose days are not complete, who lacks in his garments of Torah and mitzvos—for not every person merits this, as mentioned above—it is possible for his soul to be connected with the *Atzmus* through *teshuvah*. On the contrary, there is a merit in the connection through *teshuvah* over the connection through the garments of Torah and mitzvos. The drawing down through the garments of Torah and mitzvos is in the category of limitation, from the level of "filling all worlds." But through *teshuvah*, for *teshuvah* is in a single moment and a single instant, the drawing down through it is without limit. As explained above, the concept of *teshuvah* is shame—that any matter of measurement and limitation he knows is "black" before the Cause of all causes, and he wants to emerge from this limitation. Therefore, the drawing down through *teshuvah*, the category of "from Mitzrayim I called to My son," is a drawing down that is even more exalted.

This is "And I appeared to Avraham, to Yitzchak, and to Yaakov as Kel Shaddai..." The revelation to the Patriarchs is the category of *Kel Shaddai*, which in general is the concept of "filling all worlds." Although there are several categories in *Kel Shaddai*—there is the concept that He said to His world "enough" (*dai*), which is the nature of the world that is in the category of concealment and hiding, and there is the concept of *Kel Shaddai* above this, regarding which it is written, "And I will pour out for you a blessing until there is no *dai*," and our Sages said "until it is sufficient," which is the drawing down of *Elokus* into the worlds—nevertheless, it is only "until it is sufficient" and not the matter of wealth. As is known regarding the matter of "sufficient for his need which he lacks," even a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him—all this is only the matter of filling a lack and not the matter of wealth and luxury. That is, the drawing down from the category of "filling all worlds." However, specifically through the descent into the exile of Mitzrayim, they arrived at the revelation of the name Hashem—"from Mitzrayim I called to My son"—the drawing down from the category of Hashem, without limit, "and you shall know that I am Hashem."

This is "And Elokim spoke to Moshe and said to him, 'I am Hashem.'" This verse is a response to Moshe's question above, "Why have You done evil to this people?"—that is, why was the whole matter of the exile of Mitzrayim necessary? To this comes the response, "And said to him, 'I am Hashem,'" for the purpose of the exile of Mitzrayim is the revelation of the name Hashem. And although the name Hashem existed also for the Patriarchs as mentioned above, that is the category of Hashem of "below," the category of the name Hashem that pertains to the worlds, Hashem from the root *mehaveh* (bringing into being). However, through the descent of the exile of Mitzrayim, they arrived at the revelation of "and you shall know that I am Hashem" which is above the categories of the world, for Hashem is "He was, He is, and He will be" as one. This matter comes through the service of *teshuvah* as mentioned above, which is what is meant by "And I will give it to you as an inheritance," for the love that comes from the category of *teshuvah* is like an inheritance, where one falls into a great fortune for which he did not labor. So too, the love and closeness to Hashem that comes through *teshuvah* and shame is not through his good deeds day by day (as mentioned above), but in one hour, by way of an inheritance that comes from above. One should add further that the matter of inheritance is because the heir has a relationship to the bequeather, and the state of the heir does not matter in this; therefore, even a deaf-mute, an imbecile, or a minor inherits, because what matters is only that he has a relationship to the bequeather. This is "an inheritance, I am Hashem," for to arrive at the category of Hashem from above is through inheritance. Furthermore, "inheritance" (*morasha*) is also from the root *rosh* (head), meaning the connection with the "head of the congregation," "your heads, your tribes," for through the connection with "your heads, your tribes," even "your wood-chopper and your water-drawer" will arrive at the revelation of the name Hashem. But there must be the connection, and not to be separated, Heaven forbid, from the bequeather and the head, as mentioned above regarding *teshuvah*, which is like the son who cannot bear that his father says he is not his father, and wants to be connected to him. Through this, "and you shall know that I am Hashem," that you will be connected (*daas* is a term for connection) to the name Hashem from above, the category of "He was, He is, and He will be" as one, the category of the Infinite, all of which comes through *teshuvah*.

---
